Verbal Definition and Incomplete Description
Author explains verbal definition and discusses incomplete definition with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish verbal definition from real definition and identify incomplete description (rasm naqis).

Core Idea
Verbal definition clarifies meaning; incomplete description fails to capture essence.

Definitions serve to clarify either the meaning of a word (verbal) or the essence of a thing (real). In this passage, the author introduces verbal definition and warns against incomplete descriptions that rely on non-essential properties, such as defining 'animal' as 'laughing'. Understanding this distinction is crucial for constructing sound definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Contrast verbal and real definition
Notice that verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi) aims only to specify which meaning is attached to a term, without revealing its essence. Real definition (hadd) exposes the essential nature.
Verbal definition answers the question 'what does this word mean?' while real definition answers 'what is the essence of this thing?'
2
Examine how verbal definition works
The passage shows that verbal definition can be by a synonym (e.g., 'ghadanfar is a lion') or by a more general term (e.g., 'al-su'dana is a plant'). It does not produce new knowledge—it only clarifies.
There is no logical inference; the mind simply matches the word to its known meaning.
3
Identify why defining by a specific accident is incomplete
The example 'animal is laughing' uses a specific accident (al-'arad al-akhass) that is not part of the animal's essence. Such a definition fails to include all animals or to exclude non-animals.
This is called rasm naqis (incomplete description). The author rejects it because it defines by what is more obscure than the definiendum.
4
Recognize the author's stance against earlier scholars
Earlier scholars allowed definition by specific accident, but the author dismisses it as not beneficial. The commentary explains that the author considered it a definition by the more obscure.
The passage uses the softening phrase 'wa qad ujiza' to indicate the author's displeasure.

خاتمة مبحث التصورات ٨٦ تعريف المعرف كاللفظي، وهو ما يقصد به تفسیر مدلول اللفظ. أيضاً كتعريف الحيوان بالضاحك لكن المصنف لم يعتد به؛ لزعمه أنه تعريف بالأخفى وهو غير جائز أصلا. قوله : كاللفظي أي كما أجيز في التعريف اللفظي كونه أعم كقولهم: السعدانة نبت. قوله: تفسير مدلول اللفظ: أي تعيين مسمى اللفظ من بين المعاني المخزونة في الخاطر، فليس فيه تحصيل مجهول من معلوم كما في المعرف الحقيقي. فافهم. كتعريف الحيوان إلخ هذا التعريف رسم ناقص؛ فإن العرض الأخص لشيء خاصة غير شاملة له، والتعريف بالخاصة فقط ناقص. إسماعيل) بالضاحك والناطق؛ لأن كلا منهما عرض خارج عن حقيقة الحيوان، فلا رسم تغفل واعلم أن قول المصنف : وقد أجيز في الناقص ناقص؛ إذ لما جوز المتقدمون التعريف بالعرض الأخص كان عليه أن يقول: "وقد أجيز في الناقص أن يكون أعم وأخص وجوابه أن جواز التعريف بالأعم ليس بمرضي عند المصنف كما أشار إليه بكلمة التمريض وقد أجيز" إلخ" وقول المتقدمين بجواز التعريف بالعرض الأخص لم يكن مفيدا في نظره، فلم ينظر إليه وتركه وجعله مطروح النظر كأن لم يكن شيئا مذكورا. (عبد بتغير واختصار) لزعمه أنه تعريف بالأخفى لما مر بلا خفاء وظن أن الأخص أقل وجودا في العقل من الأعم. (عبد) نبت فإن النبت أعم من السعدانة بضم السين لنبت خاص. (إسماعيل) تحصيل مجهول بل فيه إحضار معان جزئية مخزونة في الخزانة عند المدرك مرة ثانية؛ ليتعين أن هذا المعنى قد وضع بإزاء ذلك اللفظ، فالمقصود بالتعريف اللفظي توضيح ما وضع له إما بلفظ مرادف له كقولهم: "الغضنفر أسد" وإما بلفظ أعم منه كقولهم: "السعدانة نبت. ثم اعلم أنهم اختلفوا في أن التعريف اللفظي هل من المطالب التصورية أو التصديقية؟ فذهب إلى كل ذاهب والمفهوم من الكلام الأول؛ فإنه يفهم من عبارته أن المقصود في التعريف اللفظي هو الشرح والإيضاح لا الحكم والتصديق اختار السيد السند الشريف الثاني، والحق الأول؛ فإنا إذا قلنا: الغضنفر موجود فقال المخاطب الذي لا يعلم معناه ما الغضنفر ؟ ففسرناه بالأسد، فحصل للمخاطب تصوير معناه وليس ههنا حكم أصلا ليكون تصديقا نعم فيه حكم بأن هذا اللفظ موضوع لذلك المعنى لكن موضوعية اللفظ من المباحث اللغوية لا المنطقية. (إسماعيل فافهم: إشارة إلى الاختلاف الواقع في أن التعريف اللفظي من المطالب التصورية أو التصديقية، وذهب إلى كل ذاهب واختار السيد السند الشريف الثاني، والحق هو الأول؛ لأنه يقع في جواب "ما" و"ما" يقع في جواب ما يكون تصورا؛ لأنا إذ قلنا: الغضنفر موجود ولم يفهم المخاطب معنى الغضنفر، فيسأل ما الغضنفر؟ ففسرناه الأسد، فليس هناك حكم ليكون تصديقا فيكون تصورا.
Conclusion of the section on conceptions. Definition of the definer: like the verbal, which is intended to explain the meaning of the word. Also like defining animal by 'laughing' but the author did not consider it because he claimed it is a definition by what is more obscure, and that is not permissible at all. He said: 'like the verbal' i.e., just as it was permitted in verbal definition to be more general, like their saying: 'al-su'dana is a plant.' He said: 'explanation of the meaning of the word' i.e., specifying the referent of the word from among the meanings stored in the mind, so there is no acquisition of the unknown from the known as in real definition. So understand. 'Like defining animal etc.' This definition is an incomplete description; for the specific accident of a thing is a property not inclusive of it, and definition by property only is incomplete. (Ismail) By 'laughing' and 'speaking' because each of them is an accident external to the reality of animal, so it is not a description, do not be heedless. And know that the author's saying: 'and it has been permitted in the incomplete' is incomplete; since the earlier scholars permitted definition by the specific accident, he should have said: 'and it has been permitted in the incomplete that it be more general and more specific, and its answer is that the permissibility of definition by the more general is not satisfactory to the author as he indicated by the word of softening 'and it has been permitted' etc.' And the saying of the earlier scholars about the permissibility of definition by the specific accident was not beneficial in his view, so he did not look at it and left it and made it thrown aside as if it were nothing mentioned. (Abd with change and abridgement) Because he claimed it is a definition by what is more obscure as passed without concealment, and he thought that the more specific has less existence in the mind than the more general. (Abd) 'Plant' for al-nabt is more general than al-su'dana (with damma on the sin) for a specific plant. (Ismail) 'Acquisition of the unknown' but rather in it is bringing partial meanings stored in the reservoir at the perceiver a second time, to specify that this meaning has been placed opposite that word. So the purpose of verbal definition is clarification of what it is placed for, either by a synonymous word like their saying: 'al-ghadanfar is a lion', or by a more general word like their saying: 'al-su'dana is a plant'. Then know that they differed about whether verbal definition is among conceptual demands or assensual demands? Every proponent went to something, and the understood from the first speech is that the purpose in verbal definition is explanation and clarification, not judgment and assent. Al-Sayyid al-Sanad al-Sharif the Second chose the latter, but the truth is the first; for when we say: 'al-ghadanfar exists' and the addressee who does not know its meaning asks 'what is al-ghadanfar?' and we explain it as 'lion', then the addressee obtains a mental image of its meaning, and there is no judgment here at all to be assent. Yes, there is a judgment that this word is placed for that meaning, but the positing of the word is among linguistic investigations, not logical. (Ismail) So understand: an indication of the difference that occurred about whether verbal definition is among conceptual demands or assensual demands, and every proponent went to something, and al-Sayyid al-Sanad al-Sharif the Second chose the latter, but the truth is the first; because it occurs in answer to 'ma', and 'ma' occurs in answer to what is conceptual; for when we say: 'al-ghadanfar exists' and the addressee does not understand the meaning of al-ghadanfar, then he asks 'what is al-ghadanfar?' and we explain it as 'lion', then there is no judgment to be assent, so it is conceptual.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage discusses definition (ta'rif) and its types. It begins with the category of definition that is verbal (lafzi), which aims to explain the meaning of a term by specifying its referent among stored meanings. This is contrasted with real definition (hadd), which reveals essence. The author gives an example of an incomplete definition: defining animal as 'laughing', which is rejected because it defines by something more obscure. The commentary explains that a verbal definition can be broader than the term defined, as in defining 'al-su'dana' (a specific plant) as 'naba' (plant). The passage then addresses the objection that an incomplete definition using a specific accident is not valid, noting that the specific accident is a property not inclusive of the definition, and definition by property alone is deficient. The commentary also clarifies that the author did not adopt the earlier scholars' allowance of definition by specific accident because it was not beneficial. Finally, the passage covers a scholarly dispute about whether verbal definition is conceptual (tasawwuri) or assensual (tasdiqi). The correct view is that it is conceptual because it answers 'what is it?' without any judgment; the example of 'ghadanfar' (lion) is given: when asked 'what is ghadanfar?' and we answer 'a lion', the addressee obtains a mental image, and no judgment is involved. The passage emphasizes that any judgment involved, such as that the word is placed for that meaning, belongs to linguistics, not logic.

Key Terms
تعريف لفظي
رسم ناقص
عرض أخص
غضنفر
السعدانة

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is defining 'animal' as 'laughing' considered an incomplete definition?
A) Because 'laughing' is a specific accident that does not include the entire reality of animal
B) Because 'laughing' is more obscure than 'animal'
C) Because 'laughing' is a synonym
D) Because 'animal' is a genus

Key Takeaway
A complete definition must include the essence; an incomplete description (rasm naqis) using a specific accident is deficient.

Is Verbal Definition Conceptual or Assensual?
Scholarly dispute about whether verbal definition is conceptual or assensual.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to argue whether verbal definition is conceptual (tasawwuri) or assensual (tasdiqi) and cite evidence from the passage.

Core Idea
Verbal definition is conceptual because it answers 'what is it?' without judgment.

Scholars debated whether defining a word counts as conceptual knowledge (a mental image) or assensual knowledge (a judgment). The passage argues that verbal definition is conceptual because when you explain that 'ghadanfar' means 'lion', you only provide a mental image, not a judgment. This distinction matters for understanding the scope of logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Some say verbal definition is conceptual (tasawwur), others say it is assensual (tasdiq). The passage presents both, stating that the truth is the first.
The commentator notes that al-Sayyid al-Sharif chose the assensual view, but the author disagrees.
2
Understand the argument for conceptual
The key argument: verbal definition occurs in response to the question 'what is it?' (ma). The question 'ma' seeks a mental image, not a judgment. Example: if someone asks 'what is ghadanfar?' and we answer 'a lion', no judgment is made.
A judgment would be something like 'ghadanfar exists' which is not the purpose of verbal definition.
3
Analyze the counterargument and its rebuttal
The counterargument claims that verbal definition involves a judgment that the word is placed for that meaning. The rebuttal: that judgment belongs to linguistics, not logic. Therefore, verbal definition itself remains conceptual.
Logic only concerns itself with judgments about essences, not about linguistic conventions.
4
Conclude based on the passage
The passage concludes that the correct view is that verbal definition is conceptual, as it provides a mental image without a logical judgment.
The phrase 'fafham' (so understand) signals the author's emphasis on this conclusion.

Why General Accidents Are Not Valid Definitions
Author rejects general accident as definition and allows composite of such accidents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the 'ard 'amm (general accident) is rejected as a definition and identify when a composite of general accidents can be valid.

Core Idea
A general accident reveals neither essence nor full distinction — but combined, they can specify.

In this passage, the commentator explains that logicians discarded definition by general accident because it fails the two purposes of definition: revealing the essence or distinguishing from all else. However, a collection of general accidents can produce a specific property, as in defining human as 'erect-standing walker'. Let's unpack why.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two purposes of definition
According to the text, the purpose is either to inform of the essence (كنه) or to distinguish from everything else. Write them down.
2
Test the general accident against these purposes
Does a general accident like 'walking' reveal the essence of human? Does it distinguish humans from all other animals? It falls short.
3
Understand the exception: composite of general accidents
When two general accidents are combined (e.g., erect+standing+walker), they become specific to one kind. This is considered a valid definition (composite property).
4
Apply to an Islamic example
In fiqh, defining 'salah' as 'specific actions and recitations' uses general accidents (actions, recitations) that together specify it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإلا فناقص، ولم يعتبروا بالعرض العام وقد أجيز في الناقص أن يكون أعم قوله: و لم يعتبروا بالعرض العام قالوا: الغرض من التعريف إما الإطلاع على كنه المعرّف أو امتيازه عن جميع ما عداه والعرض العام لا يفيد شيئاً منهما ؛ فلذا لم يعتبروه في مقام التعريف، والظاهر أن غرضهم من ذلك أنه لم يعتبروه انفرادا وأما التعريف بمجموع أمور كل واحد منها عرض عام للمعرَّف لكن المجموع يخصه كتعريف الإنسان بماش مستقيم القامة وتعريف الخفاش بالطائر الولود فهو تعريف بخاصة مركبة وهو معتبر عندهم كما صرح به بعض المتأخرين. قوله: وقد أجيز في الناقص أن يكون أعم إشارة إلى ما أجازه المتقدمون حيث حققوا أنه يجوز التعريف بالذاتي الأعم كتعريف الإنسان بالحيوان فيكون حداً ناقصاً أو بالعرض الأعم كتعريفه بالماشي فيكون رسما ناقصا بل جوزوا التعريف بالعرض الأخص كقولنا: الاسم كزيد والعلم كالنور والجواب أن التعريف ههنا بالحقيقة بشيء آخر لا بالمثال الأخص، فالمعنى الاسم ممثل بزيد والعلم ممثل بالنور منها: أن تعريف المعرف ههنا منقوض بالملزومات بالنسبة إلى لوازمها البينة البديهيّة؛ فإن تصوراتها مفيدة لتصور لوازمها مع أنها لم تكن معرفات؛ لما فرض من بداهة اللوازم، وأجيب: بأن المراد ما يفيد تصور الشيء بطريق النظر بقرينة أن المقصود من الفن قوانين الكسب والنظر. (خلاصة الحواشي) لم يعتبروا أي انفرادا إذ المركب من العرض العام والخاصة رسم الناقص لكنه أقوى من الخاصة ولكن المركب منه ومن الفصل حد ناقص لكنه أكمل من الفصل وحده وكذلك المركب من الفصل والخاصة حد ناقص وهو أكمل من المركب من العرض العام والفصل وأما قولهم لا حاجة إلى انضمام الخاصة إلى الفصل فمدفوع بأن التمييز الحاصل منهما معا أقوى من التمييز الحاصل بالفصل وحده. (عبد) الغرض إلخ جملة معللة لعدم الاعتبار أي المنطقيون لم يعتبروا التعريف بالعرض العام؛ لأنهم قالوا: الغرض من التعريف أحد الأمرين، وكلاهما منتف ههنا، فالتعريف عبث بالذاتي الأعم: إذ قد يكون المقصود تمييز الشيء عن بعض ما عداه، والأعم سواء كان ذاتيا أو عرضيا بل الأخص أيضاً في إفادة هذا التمييز يكون كافيا. (عبد) بالعرض الأعم: فيه إشارة إلى أن الأعم في قوله وقد أجيز في الناقص أن يكون أعم أعم. (عبد) جوزوا أي المتقدمون التعريف بالعرض الأخص لإفادته التمييز عن بعض ما عداه ووجه التخصيص بالعرض الأخص أن الذاتي إما أعم كالجنس أو عين كالنوع أو مختص كالفصل ولا يكون أخص. (عبد بزيادة)
Otherwise it is incomplete, and they did not consider the general accident, and it has been permitted in the incomplete that it be broader. His statement: 'and they did not consider the general accident' they said: the purpose of definition is either to inform of the essence of the defined or to distinguish it from everything else, and the general accident does not benefit either; therefore they did not consider it in the context of definition. And apparent is that their purpose from that is that they did not consider it singly. As for definition by a collection of matters each of which is a general accident of the defined, but the collection is specific to it, like defining human as 'erect-standing walker' and defining the bat as 'flying lactating', that is a definition by a composite property and it is considered by them, as some later scholars explicitly stated. His statement: 'and it has been permitted in the incomplete that it be broader' is an indication of what the earlier scholars allowed, where they established that it is permissible to define by the broader essential, like defining human by animal, so it is an incomplete genus, or by the broader accidental, like defining him as 'walker', so it is an incomplete description. Rather they permitted definition by the narrower accidental, like our saying: 'the noun is like Zayd' and 'Knowledge is like light.' And the answer is that the definition here is by the reality of something else, not by the narrower example, so the meaning is that the noun is represented by Zayd and knowledge is represented by light. Among them is that the definition of the defined here is refuted by the entailments with respect to their self-evident necessary consequences; for their conceptualizations are beneficial for conceptualizing their entailments, although they were not definitions, due to the assumption of the self-evidence of the entailments. And it was answered: that what is meant is what benefits the conceptualization of the thing by way of investigation, by the indication that the purpose of the art is the rules of acquisition and investigation. (Khalasat al-Hawashi): 'they did not consider' i.e., singly, for the composite of the general accident and the property is an incomplete description, but it is stronger than the property alone. And the composite of it and the differentia is an incomplete genus, but it is more complete than the differentia alone, and likewise the composite of the differentia and the property is an incomplete genus, and it is more complete than the composite of the general accident and the differentia. As for their saying 'there is no need to join the property to the differentia,' it is refuted because the distinction obtained from both together is stronger than the distinction obtained from the differentia alone. (Abd): 'The purpose etc.' is a clause giving the reason for non-consideration, i.e., the logicians did not consider definition by the general accident because they said the purpose of definition is one of two things, and both are absent here, so the definition is futile. As for the broader essential: it may be that the purpose is to distinguish the thing from some others, and the broader, whether essential or accidental, or even the narrower, can be sufficient for providing this distinction. (Abd): 'by the broader accidental' contains an indication that the 'broader' in his statement 'and it has been permitted in the incomplete that it be broader' is broader. (Abd): 'they permitted' i.e., the earlier scholars permitted definition by the narrower accidental because it provides distinction from some others, and the reason for specifying the narrower accidental is that the essential is either broader like genus, or identical like species, or specific like differentia, and it does not become narrower. (Abd with addition).
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage discusses incomplete definition (al-rasm al-naqis) and the rules governing its use. The matn states that if a definition is not complete, it is incomplete, and logicians did not consider the general accident ('ard 'amm) as a valid definition, but they did permit the incomplete definition to be broader (a'am). The commentator explains that the general accident fails to achieve the purpose of definition, which is either to reveal the essence or to distinguish the defined from all others. However, a composite of general accidents can form a specific property, e.g., defining human as 'erect-standing walker'—this is a composite property and is considered valid. The earlier scholars allowed definition by a broader essential (e.g., human as animal) as an incomplete genus, or by a broader accidental (e.g., human as walker) as an incomplete description. They even allowed definition by a narrower accidental, like 'the noun is like Zayd' or 'knowledge is like light', but the commentator clarifies that such definitions are not by the narrower example itself but by the reality of something else (the example represents the defined). The passage also addresses an objection: definitions here are refuted by the entailments because conceptualizations of self-evident entailments are beneficial, yet they are not definitions. The answer is that what is meant is beneficial conceptualization through investigation, not self-evident concepts. The commentary from Khalasat al-Hawashi and Abd further analyze the strength of composite definitions and the permissibility of using broader or narrower terms.

Key Terms
العرض العام
الرسم الناقص
الخاصة
المركب من العرض العام

Key Takeaway
The general accident is rejected singly because it fails the goals of definition, but a composite of general accidents can form a valid specific property.

Broader and Narrower Terms in Incomplete Definitions
Author permits broader and narrower terms in incomplete definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify permissible broader and narrower terms in incomplete definitions and explain the difference between essential and accidental broader terms.

Core Idea
Incomplete definitions can use broader essential or accidental terms — even narrower ones, but only by representation.

This passage reveals that earlier scholars allowed incomplete definitions to be broader than the defined, whether in essential (genus alone) or accidental (general property) terms. They even allowed narrower accidentals, but only as examples representing the defined. Let's see how this works.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between complete and incomplete definitions
Complete definitions (hadd) use genus + differentia; incomplete (rasm) use accidents. Here we focus on incomplete definitions that are broader.
2
Identify the two types of broader terms
Broader essential: e.g., defining human as 'animal' (genus alone, missing differentia). Broader accidental: e.g., defining human as 'walker' (a general accident).
3
Understand the narrower accidental
The text gives example: 'the noun is like Zayd' or 'knowledge is like light'. These are narrower examples, but the commentator clarifies they are not the definition itself but representations.
4
Apply to Islamic sciences
In fiqh, defining 'wudu' as 'washing parts' uses broader accidental (washing), but it's incomplete. Or defining 'fasting' as 'abstaining from food' is a broader essential (genus of fasting).

Source Text

(عبد) الغرض إلخ جملة معللة لعدم الاعتبار أي المنطقيون لم يعتبروا التعريف بالعرض العام؛ لأنهم قالوا: الغرض من التعريف أحد الأمرين، وكلاهما منتف ههنا، فالتعريف عبث بالذاتي الأعم: إذ قد يكون المقصود تمييز الشيء عن بعض ما عداه، والأعم سواء كان ذاتيا أو عرضيا بل الأخص أيضاً في إفادة هذا التمييز يكون كافيا. Objection: Self-Evident Entailments Are Not Definitions
Objection and response about self-evident entailments not being definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate the objection that self-evident entailments refute definitions and explain the logicians' response.

Core Idea
Self-evident entailments are not definitions because definitions require investigation, not immediate conceptualization.

The passage presents an objection: If definitions can be broader or narrower, then self-evident entailments should also count as definitions, since they give conceptualization. The logicians answer by clarifying that only definitions derived through investigation (nazar) are considered, not self-evident ones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objector says: For self-evident entailments (like fire's entailment of heat), the conceptualization of the entailment is beneficial, yet it is not considered a definition. So why allow broader accidentals?
2
Analyze the response
The response distinguishes between definitions that give conceptualization through investigation (nazar) and self-evident conceptualizations. The rules of logic (kashf wa nazar) only concern definitions obtained by investigation.
3
Apply to an Islamic example
In kalam, the existence of the world entails the existence of a creator. That entailment is self-evident to reason, but it is not considered a definition of the creator. Definitions require more detailed examination.

Classification of Definition: Hadd and Rasm
Author defines hadd and rasm and their complete/incomplete forms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given definition as a complete/incomplete hadd or rasm and explain the basis of classification.

Core Idea
Definitions are either essential (hadd) or accidental (rasm), and either complete (with proximate genus) or incomplete (without it).

In the previous lesson, you learned the condition of equality in definition. Now we apply that condition to classify definitions into four types. The author presents the criteria using the proximate genus and the quality (essential/accidental) of the distinguishing feature. Let's see how this classification works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiens components
Look at the definition and separate the elements: what is being defined (definiendum) and the properties used to define it (definiens). Note which property is the distinguishing feature.
2
Determine if the distinguishing feature is essential or accidental
If the feature is part of the essence (dhati) and cannot be removed without the thing ceasing to be what it is, it is a differentia (fasl). If it is a non-essential yet coextensive property, it is a proper accident (khassa).
Essential features are those that answer 'what is it?' – e.g., rational for human.
3
Check if the definition includes the proximate genus
The proximate genus (jins qarib) is the immediate category above the species. For example, 'animal' is the proximate genus of 'human'. If the definition includes it, it is complete; if not, it is incomplete.
A complete hadd includes both proximate genus and proximate differentia. A complete rasm includes proximate genus and proper accident.
4
Classify the definition into one of four types
Based on the previous two steps, classify as: complete hadd (essential feature + proximate genus), incomplete hadd (essential feature without proximate genus, or with remote genus), complete rasm (proper accident + proximate genus), incomplete rasm (proper accident without proximate genus).
The passage provides a systematic enumeration using binary divisions.
5
Apply the method of enumeration
Understand the logical tree: Definition → either by essentialities alone (then either all = complete hadd, or some = incomplete hadd) or not exclusively essentialities (then either includes proximate genus + proper accident = complete rasm, or other = incomplete rasm).
This enumeration ensures all possibilities are covered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتعريف بالفصل القريب حد، وبالخاصة رسم، فإن كان مع الجنس القريب فتام
قوله: بالفصل القريب: التعريف لابد له أن يشمل على أمرٍ يختص بالمعرف ويساويه بناءً على ما سبق من اشتراط المساواة، فهذا الأمر إن كان ذاتيا كان فصلا قريبا وإن كان عرضيا كان خاصة لا محالة، فعلى الأول يسمى المعرف حدا وعلى الثاني رسما، ثم كل منهما إن اشتمل على الجنس القريب يسمى حدا تاما ورسما تاما وإن لم يشتمل على الجنس القريب سواء اشتمل على الجنس البعيد أو كان هناك فصل قريب وحده أو خاصة وحدها يسمى حدا ناقصا ورسما ناقصا. هذا محصل كلامهم، وفيه أبحاث لا يسعها المقام.
حد وطريق الحصر في الأقسام الأربعة أن يقال: التعريف إما بمجرد الذاتيات أو لا، فإن كان الأول فإما أن يكون بجميع الذاتيات وهو الحد التام أو ببعضها وهو الحد الناقص، وإن كان الثاني فإما أن يكون بالجنس القريب والخاصة وهو الرسم التام أو بغير ذلك وهو الرسم الناقص.
And definition by the proximate differentia is a hadd, and by the proper accident is a rasm. If it is with the proximate genus, then it is complete.
His saying: 'by the proximate differentia': definition must necessarily include something that is specific to the definiendum and equal to it, based on the preceding condition of equality. So this thing—if it is essential, it becomes a proximate differentia; and if it is accidental, it becomes a proper accident without exception. According to the first, the definiens is called a hadd; according to the second, a rasm. Then each of them, if it includes the proximate genus, is called a complete hadd and a complete rasm; and if it does not include the proximate genus—whether it includes the remote genus, or there is only a proximate differentia alone or only a proper accident alone—it is called an incomplete hadd and an incomplete rasm. This is the summary of their statement, and in it there are investigations not accommodated by this context.
[Hadd] And the method of enumeration in the four divisions is that one says: definition is either by mere essentialities or not. If the first, then either by all essentialities—which is the complete hadd—or by some of them—which is the incomplete hadd. If the second, then either by the proximate genus and the proper accident—which is the complete rasm—or by other than that—which is the incomplete rasm.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage defines and classifies definitions (ta'rif) into two primary types: hadd (definition by essential properties) and rasm (definition by accidental properties). It then subdivides each into complete (tam) and incomplete (naqis) based on whether the proximate genus is included.

The commentator explains the rationale: a definition must include something that specifically identifies the definiendum and is coextensive with it, following the prior condition of equality. This something—if it is essential (dhati)—constitutes the proximate differentia (fasl qarib); if accidental (aradi), it constitutes the proper accident (khassa). Hence, a definiens using the former is a hadd, using the latter a rasm.

Then, each type is further divided: if the definiens includes the proximate genus (jins qarib), it is complete; if it does not, it is incomplete. An incomplete hadd or rasm may include only the remote genus, only the differentia/proper accident, or other combinations.

The passage then provides a systematic enumeration using a binary classification: definition either uses only essentialities or not. If only essentialities, either all (complete hadd) or some (incomplete hadd). If not only essentialities, then either includes proximate genus and proper accident (complete rasm) or other (incomplete rasm).

This classification is standard in post-Avicennan logic. The commentator notes that there are further investigations (abhath) not elaborated here.

الخاصة
الجنس القريب
حد تام
حد ناقص
رسم تام
رسم ناقص

Checkpoint
If one defines 'human' as 'rational animal' (nāṭiq ḥayawān), what type of definition is this according to the classification in the passage?
A) Complete hadd (ḥadd tāmm)
B) Incomplete hadd (ḥadd nāqiṣ)
C) Complete rasm (rasm tāmm)
D) Incomplete rasm (rasm nāqiṣ)

Key Takeaway
The classification of definitions into four types—complete/incomplete hadd and rasm—is based on two criteria: the nature of the distinguishing feature (essential vs. accidental) and the inclusion of the proximate genus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Classify the following definition: 'Salah is prayer consisting of specific words and actions beginning with takbir and ending with taslim.' Is it a hadd or rasm? Complete or incomplete? Explain.

Identify the proximate genus and differentia in the definition of 'Sawm' (fasting) as 'abstaining from food, drink, and sexual intercourse from dawn to sunset with intention.' Would this be a complete hadd or rasm?

The Condition of Coextensiveness (Musāwī)
Author states and explains the two essential conditions for a valid definition: coextensiveness and being better known.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine whether a given definition satisfies the condition of coextensiveness (musāwāt) by comparing the extension of definiens and definiendum.

Core Idea
The definiens must cover exactly the same things as the definiendum—no more, no less.

Now that we have defined the definiens as that which is predicated of the definiendum, it follows that it cannot be completely different. The author deduces that it must be coextensive. But what does coextensiveness mean in practice, and did all scholars agree? This lesson unpacks the first essential condition for a valid definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the logical deduction
The author argues: since the definiens is predicated of the definiendum, it cannot be mubāyin (different). It must be musāwī (coextensive). Follow this deduction.
Deduction from predication to coextensiveness.
2
Define coextensiveness
Coextensiveness means the definiens applies to exactly the same set as the definiendum. For example, if defining 'nabīdh' (a type of intoxicating drink), the definiens must apply to all nabīdh and only nabīdh.
Based on the passage: 'يجب أن يكون مساويا له'.
3
Contrast with earlier scholars
Later scholars insisted on coextensiveness, but earlier scholars allowed definitions that are more general (a‘amm) or more specific (akhass), as long as they help conception. Understand why there was a difference.
The passage notes: 'اشتراط المساواة اختيار المتأخرين والمتقدمون جوزوا التعريف بأي شيء يصلح'.
4
Test a definition
Take a definition like 'al-insān: al-ḥayawān al-nāṭiq'. Is it coextensive? Yes. But if we said 'al-insān: al-ḥayawān' (animal), it would be more general, thus not coextensive by later standards.
Apply to Islamic sciences: e.g., defining 'zakāt' as 'wājib mālī' (obligatory wealth) is not coextensive; it includes other obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قد علم من تعريف المعرّف بما يحمل على الشيء أنه لا يجوز أن يكون مباينا للمعرف فتعين أن يكون مساويا له، ثم ينبغي أن يكون أعرف من المعرَّف في نظر العقل؛ لأنه معلوم موصل إلى تصور مجهول هو المعرَّف، لا أخفى ولا مساويا له في الخفاء والظهور. بأحد الوجهين: إما بالكنه إذا كان الخاص متصور بالكنه والعام ذاتيا له فتصور الخاص بالكنه مستلزم لتصور العام بالكنه؛ إذ لو لم يحصل العام الذاتي بالكنه كيف يحصل الخاص بالكنه، وإما بالوجه إذا كان الخاص كالإنسان متصورا بالعرض العام كالماشي فيتصور العام أي الحيوان في ضمنه به؛ فإن الماشي خاصة الحيوان يميزه عن جميع ما عداه (عبد) أقل وجودا بالنظر إلى أن جهات تصوره قليلة وشرائط حصوله في العقل كثيرة بخلاف الأعم؛ فإن جهات تصوره كثيرة؛ إذ كلما يحصل الخاص في الذهن يحصل الأعم فيه أيضاً دون العكس وشرائط حصوله فيه قليلة؛ فإن جميع شرائط حصول الأعم شرائط حصول الأخص مع شرائط أخرى أيضاً عرضت له من جهة الخصوصية. (إسماعيل) في العقل: فإن وجود الخاص في العقل مستلزم لوجود العام بدون العكس، ولا يخفى عليك أن هذا الاستلزام إنما هو إذا كان العام ذاتيا للخاص ويكون الخاص معقولا بالكنه وإلا فلا، وإذا كان الأخص أقل وجودا في العقل يكون أخفى في نظره البتة. (عبد) مساويا له أي في الصدق واشتراط المساواة اختيار المتأخرين والمتقدمون جوزوا التعريف بأي شيء يصلح؛ لإفادة التصور مساويا كان أو أعم أو أخص (شوستري) لا أخفى: المراد بالأخفى ما يكون مرتبته عند العقل بعد مرتبة المعرف أسبق إلى العقل، وذلك كتعريف النار بأنه كالنفس؛ فإن النار أسبق إلى الفهم من النفس. ولا مساويا في الخفاء والظهور والمساواة في الخفاء والظهور هي أن يكون العلم بأحدهما مع العلم بالآخر والجهل بأحدهما مع الجهل بالأخر كتعريف الحركة بما ليس بسكون؛ فإنهما في المنزلة الواحدة من العلم والجهل، فمن علم أحدهما علم الآخر ومن جهل أحدهما جهل الآخر، والمعرف يجب أن يكون أقدم معرفة؛ لأنه علة لمعرفة المعرف، والعلة تكون متقدمة على المعلول . (عبد)
It is known from the definition of the definiens as that which is predicated of the thing that it is not permissible for it to be different from the definiendum, so it must be coextensive with it. Then it should be better known (a‘raf) than the definiendum in the view of the intellect; because it is known and leads to the conception of an unknown, which is the definiendum, not more obscure and not equal in obscurity and clarity. In one of two ways: either by the essence, if the particular is conceived by essence and the universal is essential to it, then the conception of the particular by essence necessitates the conception of the universal by essence; for if the essential universal is not acquired by essence, how can the particular be acquired by essence? Or by the aspect, if the particular like 'human' is conceived by an accidental universal like 'walking', then the universal, i.e., 'animal', is conceived in it by that; for 'walking' is a property of animal distinguishing it from everything else. (Abd) 'Less in existence' in view of the fact that the aspects of its conception are few and the conditions for its occurrence in the intellect are many, unlike the more general; for the aspects of its conception are many; for whenever the particular occurs in the mind, the general occurs in it also, but not vice versa, and the conditions for its occurrence are few; for all conditions for the occurrence of the general are conditions for the occurrence of the particular along with other conditions that occur to it from the aspect of particularity. (Isma‘il) 'In the intellect': for the existence of the particular in the intellect necessitates the existence of the general without the reverse, and it is not hidden from you that this necessitation is only if the general is essential to the particular and the particular is conceived by essence, otherwise not; and if the more specific is less existent in the intellect, it is necessarily more obscure in its view. (Abd) 'Coextensive to it': i.e., in truth; and the condition of coextensiveness is the choice of the later scholars, while the earlier scholars permitted definition by anything that benefits conception, whether coextensive or more general or more specific. (Shustari) 'Not more obscure': what is meant by 'more obscure' is that whose rank in the intellect is after the rank of the definiens that is more prior to the intellect, like defining fire as 'like the soul'; for fire is more prior to understanding than the soul. And 'not equal in obscurity and clarity'; and equality in obscurity and clarity is that knowledge of one is with knowledge of the other, and ignorance of one is with ignorance of the other, like defining motion as 'not rest'; for they are in the same station of knowledge and ignorance, so whoever knows one knows the other, and whoever is ignorant of one is ignorant of the other. And the definiens must be more prior in knowledge; because it is a cause for knowing the definiendum, and the cause is prior to the effect. (Abd)
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage establishes the necessary conditions for a valid definition, building on the earlier classification. It begins with a logical deduction: since the definiens (al-mu‘arrif) is predicated of the definiendum (al-mu‘arraf), it cannot be completely different (mubāyin); it must be coextensive (musāwī). Then it adds a second condition: the definiens must be better known (a‘raf) than the definiendum in the mind's estimation, because it is the known instrument that leads to the conception of the unknown definiendum. It cannot be more obscure (akhfā) nor equal in obscurity and clarity. The commentary explains how the universal can be better known in two ways: by essence (al-kunh) or by aspect (al-wajh). By essence: if the particular is conceived essentially and the universal is essential to it, then conceiving the particular essentially necessitates conceiving the universal essentially. By aspect: if the particular (e.g., human) is conceived through an accidental attribute (e.g., walking), then the universal (animal) is conceived through that attribute as a property that distinguishes it. The discussion on 'less existence' ('aqall wujūdan) clarifies that the particular is less frequent in the mind because its aspects are few and conditions many, whereas the general is more frequent and has fewer conditions. This necessitates that the particular is more obscure. The author then notes a divergence: later scholars stipulate coextensiveness, while earlier scholars allowed definition by anything that helps conception, even if more general or specific. Finally, it defines 'more obscure' and 'equal in obscurity' with examples: defining fire as 'like the soul' fails because fire is better known; defining motion as 'not rest' fails because motion and rest are equally known/unknown. The definiens must be prior in knowledge because it is the cause of knowing the definiendum. This lesson is crucial for evaluating actual definitions in the Islamic sciences, e.g., defining 'wine' as 'fermented grape juice'—if it is coextensive and better known than 'wine', it is valid.

مباين

C) al-ḥayawān al-ḍāḥik (laughing animal)
D) al-jism al-nāṭiq (rational body)

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must be coextensive with the definiendum, a condition insisted upon by later logicians to ensure precision.

Hadd and Rasm

The Condition of Being Better Known (A‘raf)
Author states and explains the two essential conditions for a valid definition: coextensiveness and being better known.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate whether a definiens is better known (a‘raf) than the definiendum, and distinguish between the two modes: by essence (kunh) and by aspect (wajh).

Core Idea
The definiens must be clearer than the definiendum; you cannot define the known by the unknown.

Even if a definition is coextensive, it is useless if it is more obscure than the definiendum. The author explains that the definiens must be better known in the intellect, and he provides two ways this can happen: by grasping the essence or through an accidental aspect. This lesson explores these concepts with examples from the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Understand the rationale
The definiens is the instrument to conceive the unknown definiendum. It must be better known; otherwise, how can it lead to knowledge? So it cannot be more obscure (akhfā) or equal in obscurity.
Based on 'لأنه معلوم موصل إلى تصور مجهول هو المعرَّف'.
2
Define 'better known' in context
Better known does not mean simpler or more basic in an absolute sense, but clearer in the mind of the learner. Example: defining 'fire' (nār) as 'like the soul' (ka-l-nafs) fails because fire is more evident than the soul.
The passage gives this example for 'more obscure'.
3
Explore the mode: by essence (kunh)
When the particular (definiendum) is conceived essentially and the universal (definiens) is essential to it, then conceiving the particular necessarily involves conceiving the universal. Example: to conceive 'human' essentially, you must conceive 'animal' essentially because 'animal' is part of the essence.
The passage says: 'تصور الخاص بالكنه مستلزم لتصور العام بالكنه'.
4
Explore the mode: by aspect (wajh)
When the particular is conceived through an accidental universal (like 'walking' for 'human'), the universal (animal) is conceived through that aspect. This is still valid because the aspect is better known than the particular in that context.
The passage says: 'إذا كان الخاص كالإنسان متصورا بالعرض العام كالماشي'.
5
Test examples
Consider defining 'nabīdh' as 'an intoxicating drink'. Is 'intoxicating drink' better known than 'nabīdh'? For a layperson, maybe not; but for a jurist, it might be. The condition is relative.
The condition is relative to the intellect of the audience.

Commentary
This passage establishes the necessary conditions for a valid definition, building on the earlier classification. It begins with a logical deduction: since the definiens (al-mu‘arrif) is predicated of the definiendum (al-mu‘arraf), it cannot be completely different (mubāyin); it must be coextensive (musāwī). Then it adds a second condition: the definiens must be better known (a‘raf) than the definiendum in the mind's estimation, because it is the known instrument that leads to the conception of the unknown definiendum. It cannot be more obscure (akhfā) nor equal in obscurity and clarity. The commentary explains how the universal can be better known in two ways: by essence (al-kunh) or by aspect (al-wajh). By essence: if the particular is conceived essentially and the universal is essential to it, then conceiving the particular essentially necessitates conceiving the universal essentially. By aspect: if the particular (e.g., human) is conceived through an accidental attribute (e.g., walking), then the universal (animal) is conceived through that attribute as a property that distinguishes it. The discussion on 'less existence' ('aqall wujūdan) clarifies that the particular is less frequent in the mind because its aspects are few and conditions many, whereas the general is more frequent and has fewer conditions. This necessitates that the particular is more obscure. The author then notes a divergence: later scholars stipulate coextensiveness, while earlier scholars allowed definition by anything that helps conception, even if more general or specific. Finally, it defines 'more obscure' and 'equal in obscurity' with examples: defining fire as 'like the soul' fails because fire is better known; defining motion as 'not rest' fails because motion and rest are equally known/unknown. The definiens must be prior in knowledge because it is the cause of knowing the definiendum. This lesson is crucial for evaluating actual definitions in the Islamic sciences, e.g., defining 'wine' as 'fermented grape juice'—if it is coextensive and better known than 'wine', it is valid.

Conditions for a Valid Definer: Equality and Being More Known
Author explains conditions for the definer: equal in extension and more known than the definiendum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to assess whether a given definer meets the two essential conditions: coextension and being more known than the definiendum.

Core Idea
A valid definer must match the definiendum's scope and be clearer in the mind.

In this passage, the author lays out the two fundamental requirements for any proper definition: the definer (al-mu'arraf) must be exactly coextensive with the definiendum (al-mu'arraf), and it must be more known (a'raf) in the mind. These conditions ensure the definition actually conveys the intended conception. We will walk through the reasoning behind these conditions and see why broader, narrower, or equally known terms fail to serve as proper definers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and definer in an example
Take a definition like 'human is rational animal'. The definiendum is 'human'; the definer is 'rational animal'. Check if the definer is exactly coextensive with the definiendum (i.e., every human is rational animal and vice versa).
Coextension means the terms apply to exactly the same set of things.
2
Test the first condition: equality in extension
Ask: Is the definer broader (a'am), narrower (akhass), or equal (musawi)? The passage states a broader term like 'animal' for 'human' fails because it does not convey the essence nor distinguish from other animals. A narrower term like 'rational' alone also fails because it is less known and insufficient.
Equality is required by later scholars; early scholars allowed any term that suffices for conception.
3
Test the second condition: being more known
The definer must be more known (a'raf) than the definiendum in the mind's view. It cannot be equally known or more hidden. For example, defining 'fire' as 'like the soul' is invalid because fire is more known than the soul. Defining 'movement' as 'what is not rest' fails because 'movement' and 'rest' are equally known.
The definer is the means to conceive the unknown; it must be prior in knowledge.
4
Determine the mode: by essence or by aspect
The passage explains that the definer conveys conception either by its essence (kannah) or by a distinguishing aspect (wajh). For instance, 'rational animal' gives the essence of human, while 'walking animal' gives an aspect. Both can work if the conditions of equality and being more known are satisfied.
Conception by essence gives access to all essential properties; conception by aspect gives a distinctive mark.

المقابلة
Conclusion of the topic of concepts. 83. Definition of the definer. Within the description of human by one of two aspects, but since the more specific has less existence in the mind and is more hidden in its view, and the function of the definer is to be more known than the definiendum, it is not permissible for it to be more specific than it. It is known from the definition of the definer as what is predicated of the thing that it is not permissible for it to be separate from the definiendum, so it is determined that it should be equal to it. Then it should be more known than the definiendum in the view of the mind, because it is a known thing leading to the conception of an unknown thing which is the definiendum, not more hidden nor equal in hiddenness and manifestness. By one of two aspects: either by essence, if the specific is conceived by essence and the universal is essential to it, then the conception of the specific by essence entails the conception of the universal by essence; for if the essential universal is not obtained by essence, how can the specific be obtained? Or by aspect, if the specific, like human, is conceived by a general accident like 'walking', then the universal, i.e. animal, is conceived within it by that; for walking is a special property of animal distinguishing it from all others. (Abd) 'Less existence' considering that its aspects of conception are few and the conditions for its obtaining in the mind are many, unlike the more general, for its aspects of conception are many; for whenever the specific obtains in the mind, the more general also obtains in it without the opposite, and the conditions for its obtaining in it are few; for all the conditions for obtaining the more general are conditions for obtaining the specific along with other conditions that also occur to it from the aspect of specificity. (Ismail) In the mind: for the existence of the specific in the mind entails the existence of the more general without the opposite, and it is not hidden from you that this entailment is only if the universal is essential to the specific and the specific is conceived by essence, otherwise not. And if the more specific has less existence in the mind, then it is more hidden in its view absolutely. (Abd) 'Equal to it' means in truthfulness, and stipulating equality is the choice of the later scholars, while the earlier scholars allowed definition by anything that suffices for conveying conception, whether equal or more general or more specific. [Shustari?] 'Not more hidden': what is meant by 'more hidden' is that whose rank in the mind is after the rank of the definer is prior to the mind; for example, defining fire as like the soul, for fire is more prior to understanding than the soul. 'Nor equal in hiddenness and manifestness': equality in hiddenness and manifestness is that knowledge of one is with knowledge of the other and ignorance of one is with ignorance of the other, like defining movement as what is not rest; for they are in the same station in knowledge and ignorance, so whoever knows one knows the other, and whoever is ignorant of one is ignorant of the other. The definer must be more prior in knowledge because it is a cause for knowledge of the definiendum, and the cause is prior to the effect. (Abd) 'Nor equal etc.' is an indication that the author's intention in his saying 'equal in knowledge' is equality in manifestness and hiddenness, considering that equality in knowledge entails equality in ignorance, that the author must say 'equal in knowledge and ignorance' as is well-known. (Ismail) So it is not refuted? [body?] Conclusion of the topic of concepts. 82. Definition of the definer. So it is not valid with the more general, the more specific, and the equal in knowledge and ignorance, and the more hidden. Either by its essence or by an aspect that distinguishes it from all others; and for this reason it is not permissible for it to be absolutely more general, because the more general does not convey either of them, like animal in defining human; for animal is not the essence of human because the reality of human is rational animal, and also it does not distinguish human from all others because some animal is the horse. Similarly, the more general from one aspect. As for the more specific, I mean absolutely, it is permissible that its conception conveys the conception of the more general by essence or by an aspect that distinguishes it from others, as when you conceive human as rational animal, you have conceived animal. = 11. And know that his saying: 'for conveying its conception' distinguishes the definer from other predicates that are predicated of subjects, for conveying the affirmation of the attribute of attributes to their subjects. (Abd) 'What is predicated etc.' in the definition of the definer there are objections: Among them is that this definition applies to genus, differentia, and species. The answer is that the definer is predicated of one thing, while these are predicated of things different in realities or agreeing. Among them is that it applies to necessary consequences relative to their evident concomitants in the more specific sense if they are intuitive. The answer is that the primary purpose of the definiendum (with kasra) is the conception of the definer (with fatha) in a way that applies to the definer (with fatha) essentially, as in its conception by essence, or accidentally, as in its conception by aspect; and necessary consequences relative to their evident concomitants in the more specific sense are not like this. Among them is that it appears from his saying 'for conveying its conception' that the definer is a cause for conveying the conception of the definiendum, and this is not the case; for we often neglect definitions and limits while the conception of the defined and limited remains, and persistence of the effect without the cause is impossible. The answer is that the definer is a final cause for conveying the conception of the definiendum, not an efficient cause. Among them is that from the apparent meaning of the definition, it is understood that predication is beneficial for the conception of the definiendum, while assent does not benefit conception. The answer is that predication is not for benefit but for obtaining assent to the affirmation of the definer of the definiendum. Among them is that this definition does not apply to verbal definition. The answer is that it is not beneficial for conception, i.e. it does not contain acquisition of an unknown from a known, so it is not a gain, so its exclusion does not harm; they mention it only as a follow-up and digression. The objections are from Ismail and most answers are derived from Abd. Either by its essence: then the intended purpose is essentially the access to all essential properties, not the distinction from all except the definiendum, even if this access entails that consideration. (Abd) Or by an aspect that distinguishes: then the intention is this distinction even if the intention is not considered. So I say: the proposition is exclusive disjunction, so it is not objected that the first entails the second, so it is not valid to object that this opposition is correct. So if you are accepting, then accept. I mean absolutely: he only interpreted the more specific by it because the more specific from one aspect falls under his saying: 'Similarly, the more general from one aspect', for the more specific from one aspect is the more general from one aspect. (Ismail) The opposition.

Commentary
This passage is a definitional explanation of the conditions that the definer (al-mu'arraf) must satisfy in a proper definition. The author begins by stating that the definer must be more known (a'raf) than the definiendum (al-mu'arraf). It cannot be more specific (akhass) because the more specific has less existence in the mind and is more hidden, while the definer should be clearer. The definer also cannot be separate (mubayin) from the definiendum; it must be equal (musawi) in extension. Then it must be more known in the view of the mind, as it is a means to conceive the unknown definiendum. The definer can be known in two ways: either by essence (kannah) if the specific is conceived through its essence, which entails conception of the universal, or by aspect (wajh) if the specific is conceived through a general accident, like 'walking' for human, which then conveys animal. The author clarifies that the more specific has fewer aspects of conception but more conditions, while the more general has more aspects but fewer conditions. Equality in hiddenness and manifestness is problematic because if two terms are equally known, defining one by the other would not help. The passage then addresses objections to the definition of the definer, such as that it applies to genus, differentia, and species, but the answer is that the definer is predicated of one thing while these are predicated of different things. Also, the claim that the definer is a cause for conception is countered by saying it is a final cause, not an efficient cause, and that predication yields assent, not conception. The passage concludes with a discussion on whether the definer's purpose is essence or distinction, and explains that the exclusive disjunction (man'iat al-khuluww) prevents the objection that one entails the other.

Key Takeaway
A valid definer must be exactly coextensive with the definiendum and more known in the mind, conveying conception either through essence or through a distinguishing aspect.

Conditions of a Valid Definer
Author defines the definer and its conditions, with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a proposed definer is valid by checking if it is clearer and reveals essence or distinction.

Core Idea
A valid definer must be clearer and either give essence or unique mark.

In this passage, the author sets the rules for what can serve as a definer (al-mu'arraf). A proper definition must use terms that are clearer than the defined, and must either capture its essence or its distinguishing feature. You will learn why general terms fail and when specific terms can help.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definer and the defined
In the example 'human defined as animal', the definer is 'animal' and the defined is 'human'.
2
Check if the definer is clearer or more known
The definer must be more apparent (ajla) than the defined. 'Animal' is more general and thus more known, so it passes the clarity test.
3
Check if definer gives essence or distinct mark
The definer must either give the essence (kunnah) of the defined or a mark that distinguishes it from all else. The passage says 'animal' fails because it is neither the essence (kunnah) of human nor does it distinguish humans from horses.
4
Apply to more specific terms
A more specific term (akhass) like 'rational animal' can be a valid definer because it gives the essence of 'human' and also distinguishes it, thus allowing conception of the more general 'animal'.

خاتمة مبحث التصورات ۸۲ تعريف المعرف فلا يصح بالأعم والأخص والمساوي معرفةً وجهالة والأخفى إما بكنهه أو بوجه يمتاز عن جميع ما عداه؛ ولهذا لم يجز أن يكون أعم مطلقا؛ لأن الأعم لا يفيد شيئا منهما كالحيوان في تعريف الإنسان؛ فإن الحيوان ليس بكنه الإنسان لأن حقيقة الإنسان هو الحيوان الناطق، وأيضاً لا يميز الإنسان عن جميع ما عداه؛ لأن بعض الحيوان هو الفرس، وكذا الحال في الأعم من وجه وأما الأخص أعني مطلقا فهو وإن جاز أن يفيد تصوره تصور الأعم بالكنه أو بوجه يمتاز به عما عداه كما إذا تصورت الإنسان بأنه حيوان ناطق فقد تصورت الحيوان
Conclusion of the topic of concepts (tasawwurat). Definition of the definer (al-mu'arraf): It is not valid [to define] with the more general (a'amm), the more specific (akhass), or the equal (musawi) as a definition or description, and [it must be] clearer [than the defined]. Either by its essence (kunnah) or by a distinguishing mark (wajh) that distinguishes it from all else. Therefore, it is not permissible for it to be absolutely more general because the more general does not yield either of the two — like 'animal' in the definition of 'human'; for 'animal' is not the essence of 'human' because the reality of 'human' is 'rational animal', and also it does not distinguish 'human' from all others because some animal is the horse. Similarly for the more general from one perspective (a'amm min wajh). As for the more specific, i.e., absolutely, it is possible that its concept yields the concept of the more general by essence or by a distinguishing mark, as when you conceive 'human' as 'rational animal' you have conceived 'animal'.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the definer (al-mu'arraf) from a commentary on the topic of concepts. It states that a proper definition must not be formulated using terms that are more general (a'amm), more specific (akhass), or equal (musawi) to the defined term. Instead, the definer must be clearer (ajla) than the defined. The definition must either provide the essence (kunnah) of the thing or a distinguishing feature (wajh) that separates it from everything else. The author explains why a more general term fails: it does not give the essence nor does it uniquely distinguish. For example, defining 'human' as 'animal' is insufficient because 'animal' is not the essence of 'human' (which is rational animal) and also includes other animals like horses. Similarly, a term that is more general from one perspective (a'amm min wajh) suffers the same defect. However, a more specific term (akhass mutlaq) can be used if it helps conceive the more general term, as when 'rational animal' leads one to conceive 'animal'.

Key Terms
المعرف
الأعم
الأخص
الكنه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can 'animal' not serve as the definition of 'human'?
A) Because 'animal' is more specific than 'human'.
B) Because 'animal' is not the essence of 'human' and does not distinguish humans from other animals.
C) Because 'animal' is equal in meaning to 'human'.
D) Because 'animal' is a synonym for 'human'.

Key Takeaway
A valid definer must be clearer than the defined and must either give the essence or a distinguishing feature; more general terms fail both requirements.

Testing Definitions Through Objections
Author lists objections to the definition of al-mu'arraf and provides responses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to test a definition by identifying and evaluating objections similar to those applied to the definer in this passage.

Core Idea
A definition is refined by testing it against objections that challenge its scope, necessity, and clarity.

In this passage, the author systematically addresses five objections to the definition of 'the definer' (al-mu'arraf). Each objection targets a different aspect: coverage, purpose, causality, relation to assent, and verbal definitions. By following the logical responses, you will learn how to defend and refine a definition using precise distinctions. This skill is directly transferable to any definition in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition under scrutiny
Locate the definition of al-mu'arraf in the passage: 'ما يحمل لإفادة تصور الموضوع' (what is predicated to benefit the conception of the subject). This is the target of all objections.
2
List the five objections
Read through each objection: (1) applies to genus/differentia, (2) applies to necessary concomitants, (3) implies definer is a cause, (4) predication gives assent not conception, (5) excludes verbal definition. For each, understand what part of the definition it challenges.
Objectors are from two figures: Isma'il and Abd.
3
Analyze the responses
For each objection, see how the author refines the definition: (1) definer predicated of one thing; (2) primary purpose is essential conception not mere implication; (3) definer is purpose, not cause; (4) predication obtains assent, but the definition refers to the conceptual benefit; (5) verbal definitions are subsidiary and not acquisitional.
Notice the key distinction between cause ('illa) and purpose (ghaya).
4
Recognize the refinement technique
The objections force the author to clarify what is 'essential' vs. 'incidental' in the definition. The final discussion on 'by essence' (kunnah) vs. 'by distinguishing mark' (wajh) shows that the definer serves different primary purposes, but the proposition is 'mani'at al-khuluw'—at least one must be intended.
This logical tool is critical in dialetical refinement.
5
Apply to an Islamic science definition
Now take a definition from usul al-fiqh, e.g., 'Qiyas is extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause (illa).' Test it with analogous objections: Does it apply to other types of reasoning? Is the cause or purpose? Does it require assent? Does it include analogies that don't produce new knowledge?

And know that his saying: 'to benefit its conception' separates the definer from other predicates that are predicated of subjects, to benefit the establishment of attributes of attributes for their subjects. (Abd) 'what is predicated etc.' in the definition of the definer has objections: among them, that this definition applies to genus, differentia, and species. The answer: the definer is predicated of one thing, while these are predicated of things that are different in reality or similar. Among them, that it applies to the necessitants (malzumāt) with respect to their necessary concomitants (lawāzim) that are clear in the more specific sense if they are self-evident. The answer: the primary purpose of the definer (with kasr) is the conception of the defined (with fath) in a way that corresponds to the defined by essence as in conceiving it by essence, or by accident as in conceiving it by a distinguishing mark. Their relation to their necessary concomitants is not like this. Among them, that it appears from his saying 'to benefit its conception' that the definer is a cause (illa) for benefiting the conception of the defined, but this is not the case; for we often forget the descriptions and definitions while the conception of the described and defined remains, and the persistence of the required without the cause is impossible. The answer: the definer is a purpose (ghaya) for benefiting the conception of the defined, not a cause. Among them, that it is understood from the apparent meaning of the definition that predication benefits the conception of the defined, but assent (tasdiq) does not benefit conception. The answer: predication is not for benefit but for obtaining assent to the establishment of the definer for the defined. Among them, that this definition does not apply to verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi). The answer: it is not beneficial for conception, i.e., it does not acquire an unknown from a known, so it is not a kasb (acquisition), so its exclusion does no harm, and they only mention it as a subsidiary and digression. The objections are from Isma'il, and most answers are derived from Abd. 'Either by its essence' — then the primary purpose is to apprehend all essential properties, not distinction from all except the defined, although this apprehension entails that consideration. (Abd) 'Or by a distinguishing mark' — then the intention is this distinction, even if the intention is not considered. So I say: the proposition is a preventive of emptiness (mani'at al-khuluw), so it is not objected that the first entails the second, so it is invalid to object that this contrast is correct. So if you are accepting, then accept. 'I mean absolutely' — he only interpreted 'the more specific' with it because the more specific from one perspective is included under his saying: 'Similarly for the more general from one perspective', since the more specific from one perspective is the more general from one perspective. (Isma'il) The contrast.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a critical discussion of objections (iradat) raised against a previous definition of the definer (al-mu'arraf). The author first clarifies that the phrase 'to benefit its conception' separates the definer from other predicates. Then he lists several objections. The first objection is that the definition applies to genus, differentia, and species, but the response is that the definer is predicated of one thing, while those are predicated of different things. The second objection concerns necessary concomitants (lawāzim) that are clear; the response emphasizes that the primary purpose of the definer is to provide conception of the defined by essence or by distinguishing mark, which is not the case for necessary concomitants. The third objection argues that the definer appears to be a cause (illa) of conception, but we often forget the definer while retaining conception of the defined; the response clarifies that the definer is a purpose (ghaya), not a cause. The fourth objection points out that predication (haml) gives assent (tasdiq), not conception (tasawwur), so the phrase 'to benefit its conception' is problematic; the response says predication is not for benefiting conception but for establishing assent. The fifth objection concerns verbal definitions; the response says they are not true definitions since they do not provide new knowledge. Then the author discusses the two ways of definition: by essence (kunnah) or by distinguishing mark (wajh). He argues that the first entails the second, but the proposition is 'mani'at al-khuluw' (preventive of emptiness), meaning that at least one must be intended. Finally, he clarifies that 'the more specific absolutely' (al-akhass al-mutlaq) is interpreted as such because the more specific from one perspective is actually a form of the more general from one perspective.

المحمولات
الملزومات
اللوازم البينة
غاية
مانعة الخلو

Key Takeaway
The definition of the definer is preserved by clarifying that it is a purpose (ghaya) for conception, not a cause, and that it covers both essential and distinguishing definitions.

The Definition of the Definer and the Problem of Universals
Definition of the definer and discussion on universal existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the definition of the definer and analyze the argument against the external existence of universals.

Core Idea
The definer is a predicate for conception, but universals cannot exist externally without contradiction.

This passage from Tahdhib al-Mantiq presents the definition of the definer (al-mu'arraf) and immediately addresses a metaphysical problem: if universals existed externally, one thing would have opposing attributes. The commentator explains the conditions of definition and resolves the issue by clarifying the role of predication.

Guided Path
1
Extract the formal definition of al-mu'arraf
The definer is what is predicated to benefit conception, with conditions of equality or clarity. Locate this in the Arabic text.
2
Analyze the argument against universals
The commentator argues that if universals existed externally in their individuals, one thing would have contradictory attributes (universality and particularity) and exist in multiple places, which is impossible.
This is a conditional argument: if external existence, then impossible consequences.
3
Understand the proposed solution
The natural universal (al-tabi'i) exists only in the sense that its individuals exist; it does not exist as a separate entity.
4
Examine the counter-argument and refutation
Some object that universals can exist as types (e.g., human nature), but the commentator refutes: existence entails personal essence, not shared nature, leading to contradiction.
5
Clarify the role of predication
Primary purpose of the definer is conception (tasawwur), but predication is necessary to obtain assent (tasdiq); it is accidental, not essential.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Conclusion of the topic of concepts. Chapter: Definition of the definer. The definer of a thing is what is predicated of it to benefit its conception, and it is required that it be equal or clearer. ... And among them is the author; therefore he said: 'And the truth is the second' — because if the universal existed externally within its individuals, then one thing would be characterized by opposing attributes like universality and particularity, and one thing would exist in multiple places. And then the meaning of the existence of the natural (tabi'i) is that its individuals exist. And in it there is reflection (ta'ammul), and the verification of the truth is in the marginalia of al-Tajrid, so look into it. His saying: 'Definer of a thing': After finishing the explanation of what the definer is composed of, he began the investigation into it. And you know that the primary purpose in this art is the investigation into it and into the proof (hujja). And he defined it as: 'What is predicated of a thing, i.e., the defined, to benefit the conception of this thing.' This is the report that the interpretation of the author's saying 'meaning the existence of its individuals' is a reconciliation between the two opinions, by the author: and it appears that the interpretation of some is very weak. And in it there is reflection, etc., indicating what the commentator of al-Tajrid transmitted from some: that the characterization of one thing with opposing attributes and its existence in multiple places is only impossible if the thing is one in person (shakhs), but if it is one in type (naw'), then it is not. So human nature, for example, exists externally and is subject to multiple individuations; it has individuals existing externally, and it is common existing in all of them without individuation, and with respect to each individual it is characterized by a specific attribute and located in a specific place, and there is no impossibility in that. And it is possible to respond: we know with certainty that everything that exists externally is characterized by itself, not subject to sharing — human nature, on the assumption that it exists externally specified by itself irrespective of what occurs to it, how can it be common among individuals characterized by opposing attributes with respect to the individuals existing in multiple places through it? Rather, its being external necessitates that it be a personal essence. This is a contradiction. (Abd) 'What is predicated, etc.' is an indication that 'al-maqul' in the text means 'al-mahmul' (the predicate) because it is transitive with 'ala'. And it is not hidden that the primary purpose of the definer (with kasr) is the conception of the defined (with fath) in a way that corresponds to the defined by essence as in conceiving it by essence, or by accident as in conceiving it by a distinguishing mark. And this does not contradict predication; rather, predication is necessary to obtain assent to its establishment, otherwise it would not be a mirror for observation. But that predication is not intended by essence but by accident. Therefore they said: Mentioning the definer is not necessary in the definition; it is only mentioned to bring it to mind and the definition is predicated of it to benefit unification (ittihad) in some respect.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a definition of the definer (al-mu'arraf) from the matn. It begins by stating a standard definition: 'The definer of a thing is what is predicated of it to benefit its conception, and it must be equal or clearer.' Then it discusses an author (al-musannif) who says the truth is the second opinion (al-haqq huwa al-thani). This leads into a metaphysical argument about the existence of universals. If universals existed externally within their individuals, then one thing would have contradictory attributes (e.g., universality and particularity) and could be in multiple places. The natural universal (tabi'i) exists only in the sense that its individuals exist. There is a reflection (ta'ammul) on this. The commentator notes that the resolution is in the marginalia of al-Tajrid. Then the commentary explains the matn phrase 'what is predicated' and clarifies that the primary purpose of the definer is conception, not predication itself. Predication is necessary to produce assent (tasdiq) that the definer applies to the defined, but the predication is accidental, not essential. The definer is mentioned to bring the defined to mind, and the definition is predicated of the defined to indicate a certain unity (ittihad).

الكلي
الطبيعي
المحمول
الحمل

Key Takeaway
